java.util.Set;\\n48: import java.util.regex.Pattern;\\n49: \\n50: import static org.apache.kafka.common.utils.Utils.propsToMap;\\n51: \\n52: /**\\n53:  * A client that consumes records from a Kafka cluster.\\n54:  * <p>\\n55:  * This client transparently handles the failure of Kafka brokers, and transparently adapts as topic partitions\\n56:  * it fetches migrate within the cluster. This client also interacts with the broker to allow groups of\\n57:  * consumers to load balance consumption using <a href=\\\"#consumergroups\\\">consumer groups</a>.\\n58:  * <p>\\n59:  * The consumer maintains TCP connections to the necessary brokers to fetch data.\\n60:  * Failure to close the consumer after use will leak these connections.\\n61:  * The consumer is not thread-safe. See <a href=\\\"#multithreaded\\\">Multi-threaded Processing</a> for more details.\\n62:  *\\n63:  * <h3>Cross-Version Compatibility</h3>\\n64:  * This client can communicate with brokers that are version 0.10.0 or newer. Older or newer brokers may not support\\n65:  * certain features. For example, 0.10.0 brokers do not support offsetsForTimes, because this feature was added\\n66:  * in version 0.10.1. You will receive an {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.UnsupportedVersionException}\\n67:  * when invoking an API that is not available on the running broker version.\\n68:  * <p>\\n69:  *\\n70:  * <h3>Offsets and Consumer Position</h3>\\n71:  * Kafka maintains a numerical offset for each record in a partition. This offset acts as a unique identifier of\\n72:  * a record within that partition, and also denotes the position of the consumer in the partition. For example, a consumer\\n73:  * which is at position 5 has consumed records with offsets 0 through 4 and will next receive the record with offset 5.\\n74:  * Note that offsets are not guaranteed to be consecutive (such as compacted topic or when records have been produced\\n75:  * using transactions). For example, if the consumer did read a record with offset 4, but 5 is not an offset\\n76:  * with a record, its position might advance to 6 (or higher) directly. Similarly, if the consumer's position is 5,\\n77:  * but there is no record with offset 5, the consumer will return the record with the next higher offset.\\n78:  * There are actually two notions of position relevant to the user of the consumer:\\n79:  * <p>\\n80:  * The {@link #position(TopicPartition) position} of the consumer gives the offset of the next record that will be given\\n81:  * out. It will be one larger than the highest offset the consumer has seen in that partition. It automatically advances\\n82:  * every time the consumer receives messages in a call to {@link #poll(Duration)}.\\n83:  * <p>\\n84:  * The {@link #commitSync() committed position} is the last offset that has been stored securely. Should the\\n85:  * process fail and restart, this is the offset that the consumer will recover to. The consumer can either automatically commit\\n86:  * offsets periodically; or it can choose to control this committed position manually by calling one of the commit APIs\\n87:  * (e.g. {@link #commitSync() commitSync} and {@link #commitAsync(OffsetCommitCallback) commitAsync}).\\n88:  * <p>\\n89:  * This distinction gives the consumer control over when a record is considered consumed. It is discussed in further\\n90:  * detail below.\\n91:  *\\n92:  * <h3><a name=\\\"consumergroups\\\">Consumer Groups and Topic Subscriptions</a></h3>\\n93:  *\\n94:  * Kafka uses the concept of <i>consumer groups</i> to allow a pool of processes to divide the work of consuming and\\n95:  * processing records. Structure\\nThe primary public API is `KafkaConsumer` (sg-evals/kafka--0753c489:clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java), which acts as a facade delegating to internal implementations through the `ConsumerDelegate` interface (sg-evals/kafka--0753c489:clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerDelegate.java). This interface extends the `Consumer` contract (sg-evals/kafka--0753c489:clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/Consumer.java), which defines offset management methods: `commitSync()`, `commitAsync()`, `position()`, `seek()`, and `committed()`.\\n\\n## Implementation Strategies\\n\\n### Classic Implementation (Pre-KIP 848)\\nThe `ClassicKafkaConsumer` (sg-evals/kafka--0753c489:clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ClassicKafkaConsumer.java) implements the legacy group protocol with synchronous network I/O. All blocking operations (poll, metadata fetches, offset commits) execute in the application thread. It uses `ConsumerCoordinator`, `Fetcher<K,V>`, and `OffsetFetcher` components for managing group coordination and offset tracking. Offset management is direct: `commitSync()` and `commitAsync()` immediately communicate with brokers through `ConsumerNetworkClient`.\\n\\n### Async Implementation (KIP-848)\\nThe `AsyncKafkaConsumer` (sg-evals/kafka--0753c489:clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/AsyncKafkaConsumer.java) implements the new consumer group protocol using an event-driven architecture. An `ApplicationEventHandler` processes `ApplicationEvent` instances (including `CommitEvent`, `SeekEvent`, `PollEvent`) asynchronously through a dedicated `ConsumerNetworkThread`. This decouples application thread operations from network I/O. The implementation uses `CommitRequestManager` for managing offset commits and includes `SubscriptionState` for tracking partition positions and offsets.\\n\\n## Key Behavioral Differences in Offset Management\\n\\n### Position Tracking\\n- **ClassicKafkaConsumer**: Maintains position through `SubscriptionState` accessed directly during `poll()` calls. Position automatically advances as records are fetched and returned.\\n- **AsyncKafkaConsumer**: Maintains position through event-based state management. `position()` calls trigger a `FetchPositionEvent` processed asynchronously through the event handler, returning the current position from `SubscriptionState`.\\n\\n### Offset Commits\\n- **ClassicKafkaConsumer**: `commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>)` at lines 735-738 and `commitAsync()` at lines 768+ execute synchronously with the application thread. The synchronous variant (line 736-737) wraps with a Duration-based timeout and calls the underlying coordinator.\\n- **AsyncKafkaConsumer**: `commitSync()` at lines 1581-1583 and `commitAsync()` at lines 896-898 convert offset maps to optional and delegate to internal `commitSync/commitAsync` methods which submit `CommitEvent` instances to the `applicationEventHandler`. These methods return `CompletableFuture<Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>>` for async execution.\\n\\n### Committed Offset Retrieval\\n- **ClassicKafkaConsumer** (lines 882-888): `committed()` calls fetch committed offsets synchronously from the broker using `ConsumerCoordinator`.\\n- **AsyncKafkaConsumer** (lines 1043-1051): `committed()` submits an async event to fetch committed offsets, with the result obtained through `OffsetCommitMetricsManager`.\\n\\n## Offset Management Patterns in Consumer Integrations\\n\\nCamel's Kafka integration (sg-evals/camel--1006f047:components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/AbstractCommitManager.java) demonstrates practical offset management. The `forceCommit()` method (lines 85-95) uses `consumer.commitSync(Collections.singletonMap(partition, new OffsetAndMetadata(partitionLastOffset + 1)), Duration.ofMillis(timeout))`. This pattern shows that offsets are committed as the next offset to be consumed (lastOffset + 1), aligning with the API contract that committed offsets represent the next message to fetch.\\n\\n## Migration Path and Compatibility\\nThe `KafkaConsumer` public API maintains backward compatibility by supporting both implementations internally. The `GroupProtocol` configuration (CLASSIC vs CONSUMER) determines which delegate is instantiated. ClassicKafkaConsumer remains for pre-KIP 848 compatibility, while AsyncKafkaConsumer represents the future direction with improved threading model and resource efficiency. internal implementations through the `ConsumerDelegate` interface (sg-evals/kafka--0753c489:clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerDelegate.java). This interface extends the `Consumer` contract (sg-evals/kafka--0753c489:clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/Consumer.java), which defines offset management methods: `commitSync()`, `commitAsync()`, `position()`, `seek()`, and `committed()`.\\n\\n## Implementation Strategies\\n\\n### Classic Implementation (Pre-KIP 848)\\nThe `ClassicKafkaConsumer` (sg-evals/kafka--0753c489:clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ClassicKafkaConsumer.java) implements the legacy group protocol with synchronous network I/O. All blocking operations (poll, metadata fetches, offset commits) execute in the application thread. It uses `ConsumerCoordinator`, `Fetcher<K,V>`, and `OffsetFetcher` components for managing group coordination and offset tracking. Offset management is direct: `commitSync()` and `commitAsync()` immediately communicate with brokers through `ConsumerNetworkClient`.\\n\\n### Async Implementation (KIP-848)\\nThe `AsyncKafkaConsumer` (sg-evals/kafka--0753c489:clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/AsyncKafkaConsumer.java) implements the new consumer group protocol using an event-driven architecture. An `ApplicationEventHandler` processes `ApplicationEvent` instances (including `CommitEvent`, `SeekEvent`, `PollEvent`) asynchronously through a dedicated `ConsumerNetworkThread`. This decouples application thread operations from network I/O. The implementation uses `CommitRequestManager` for managing offset commits and includes `SubscriptionState` for tracking partition positions and offsets.\\n\\n## Key Behavioral Differences in Offset Management\\n\\n### Position Tracking\\n- **ClassicKafkaConsumer**: Maintains position through `SubscriptionState` accessed directly during `poll()` calls. Position automatically advances as records are fetched and returned.\\n- **AsyncKafkaConsumer**: Maintains position through event-based state management. `position()` calls trigger a `FetchPositionEvent` processed asynchronously through the event handler, returning the current position from `SubscriptionState`.\\n\\n### Offset Commits\\n- **ClassicKafkaConsumer**: `commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>)` at lines 735-738 and `commitAsync()` at lines 768+ execute synchronously with the application thread. The synchronous variant (line 736-737) wraps with a Duration-based timeout and calls the underlying coordinator.\\n- **AsyncKafkaConsumer**: `commitSync()` at lines 1581-1583 and `commitAsync()` at lines 896-898 convert offset maps to optional and delegate to internal `commitSync/commitAsync` methods which submit `CommitEvent` instances to the `applicationEventHandler`. These methods return `CompletableFuture<Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>>` for async execution.\\n\\n### Committed Offset Retrieval\\n- **ClassicKafkaConsumer** (lines 882-888): `committed()` calls fetch committed offsets synchronously from the broker using `ConsumerCoordinator`.\\n- **AsyncKafkaConsumer** (lines 1043-1051): `committed()` submits an async event to fetch committed offsets, with the result obtained through `OffsetCommitMetricsManager`.\\n\\n## Offset Management Patterns in Consumer Integrations\\n\\nCamel's Kafka integration (sg-evals/camel--1006f047:components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/AbstractCommitManager.java) demonstrates practical offset management. This pattern shows that offsets are committed as the next offset to be consumed (lastOffset + 1), aligning with the API contract that committed offsets represent the next message to fetch.\\n\\n## Migration Path and Compatibility\\nThe `KafkaConsumer` public API maintains backward compatibility by supporting both implementations internally. The `GroupProtocol` configuration (CLASSIC vs CONSUMER) determines which delegate is instantiated. ClassicKafkaConsumer remains for pre-KIP 848 compatibility, while AsyncKafkaConsumer represents the future direction with improved threading model and resource efficiency. Both implement identical offset management contracts through the Consumer interface, ensuring application-level transparency despite implementation differences.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
